      <p>
       <b>
        Rhodes
       </b>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">
        Greek
       </a>
       :
       <span lang="el" xml:lang="el">
        Ρόδος
       </span>
       ,
       <i>
        Ródos
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Greek" title="Help:IPA/Greek">
         [ˈroðos]
        </a>
       </span>
       ) is the largest of the
       <a href="/wiki/Dodecanese" title="Dodecanese">
        Dodecanese
       </a>
       islands of
       <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">
        Greece
       </a>
       in terms of land area and also the island group's historical capital. Administratively the island forms a separate municipality within the
       <a href="/wiki/Rhodes_(regional_unit)" title="Rhodes (regional unit)">
        Rhodes regional unit
       </a>
       , which is part of the
       <a href="/wiki/South_Aegean" title="South Aegean">
        South Aegean
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Administrative_regions_of_Greece" title="Administrative regions of Greece">
        administrative region
       </a>
       . The principal town of the island and seat of the municipality is
       <a href="/wiki/Rhodes_(city)" title="Rhodes (city)">
        Rhodes
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kallikratis_2-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Kallikratis-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The city of Rhodes had 50,636 inhabitants in 2011. It is located northeast of
       <a href="/wiki/Crete" title="Crete">
        Crete
       </a>
       , southeast of
       <a href="/wiki/Athens" title="Athens">
        Athens
       </a>
       and just off the Anatolian coast of
       <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">
        Turkey
       </a>
       . Rhodes' nickname is
       <i>
        The island of the Knights
       </i>
       , named after the
       <a href="/wiki/Knights_Hospitaller" title="Knights Hospitaller">
        Knights of Saint John of Jerusalem
       </a>
       , who once conquered the land.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Historically, Rhodes was famous worldwide for the
       <a href="/wiki/Colossus_of_Rhodes" title="Colossus of Rhodes">
        Colossus of Rhodes
       </a>
       , one of the
       <a href="/wiki/Seven_Wonders_of_the_Ancient_World" title="Seven Wonders of the Ancient World">
        Seven Wonders of the Ancient World
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Fortifications_of_Rhodes" title="Fortifications of Rhodes">
        The Medieval Old Town of the City of Rhodes
       </a>
       has been declared a
       <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">
        World Heritage Site
       </a>
       . Today, it is one of the most popular tourist destinations in Europe.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Name">
        Name
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rhodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Name">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The island has been known as Ρόδος in Greek throughout its history. In addition, the island has been called Rodi in
       <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">
        Italian
       </a>
       , Rodos in
       <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">
        Turkish
       </a>
       , and
       <i>
        Rodi
       </i>
       or
       <i>
        Rodes
       </i>
       in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ladino_language" title="Ladino language">
        Ladino
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Travels_of_Sir_John_Mandeville" title="The Travels of Sir John Mandeville">
         The Travels of Sir John Mandeville
        </a>
       </i>
       incorrectly reports that Rhodes was formerly called "Collosus", through a conflation of the Colossus of Rhodes and
       <a href="/wiki/Paul_the_Apostle" title="Paul the Apostle">
        Paul
       </a>
       's
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Epistle_to_the_Colossians" title="Epistle to the Colossians">
         Epistle to the Colossians
        </a>
       </i>
       , which refers to
       <a href="/wiki/Colossae" title="Colossae">
        Colossae
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">
        Geography
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rhodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rhodos_topo.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1496" data-file-width="1500" height="180" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Rhodos_topo.png/180px-Rhodos_topo.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Rhodos_topo.png/270px-Rhodos_topo.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Rhodos_topo.png/360px-Rhodos_topo.png 2x" width="180"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rhodos_topo.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Topographic map of Rhodes.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Akramitis.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="950" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Akramitis.jpg/200px-Akramitis.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Akramitis.jpg/300px-Akramitis.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Akramitis.jpg/400px-Akramitis.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Akramitis.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Akramitis mountain
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ixia_beach_Rhodes_Greece_2.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Ixia_beach_Rhodes_Greece_2.jpg/200px-Ixia_beach_Rhodes_Greece_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Ixia_beach_Rhodes_Greece_2.jpg/300px-Ixia_beach_Rhodes_Greece_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Ixia_beach_Rhodes_Greece_2.jpg/400px-Ixia_beach_Rhodes_Greece_2.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ixia_beach_Rhodes_Greece_2.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Ixia beach, Rhodes
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%CE%97_%CE%BA%CE%BF%CE%B9%CE%BB%CE%AC%CE%B4%CE%B1_%CF%84%CF%89%CE%BD_%CF%80%CE%B5%CF%84%CE%B1%CE%BB%CE%BF%CF%8D%CE%B4%CF%89%CE%BD.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/%CE%97_%CE%BA%CE%BF%CE%B9%CE%BB%CE%AC%CE%B4%CE%B1_%CF%84%CF%89%CE%BD_%CF%80%CE%B5%CF%84%CE%B1%CE%BB%CE%BF%CF%8D%CE%B4%CF%89%CE%BD.jpg/200px-%CE%97_%CE%BA%CE%BF%CE%B9%CE%BB%CE%AC%CE%B4%CE%B1_%CF%84%CF%89%CE%BD_%CF%80%CE%B5%CF%84%CE%B1%CE%BB%CE%BF%CF%8D%CE%B4%CF%89%CE%BD.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/%CE%97_%CE%BA%CE%BF%CE%B9%CE%BB%CE%AC%CE%B4%CE%B1_%CF%84%CF%89%CE%BD_%CF%80%CE%B5%CF%84%CE%B1%CE%BB%CE%BF%CF%8D%CE%B4%CF%89%CE%BD.jpg/300px-%CE%97_%CE%BA%CE%BF%CE%B9%CE%BB%CE%AC%CE%B4%CE%B1_%CF%84%CF%89%CE%BD_%CF%80%CE%B5%CF%84%CE%B1%CE%BB%CE%BF%CF%8D%CE%B4%CF%89%CE%BD.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/%CE%97_%CE%BA%CE%BF%CE%B9%CE%BB%CE%AC%CE%B4%CE%B1_%CF%84%CF%89%CE%BD_%CF%80%CE%B5%CF%84%CE%B1%CE%BB%CE%BF%CF%8D%CE%B4%CF%89%CE%BD.jpg/400px-%CE%97_%CE%BA%CE%BF%CE%B9%CE%BB%CE%AC%CE%B4%CE%B1_%CF%84%CF%89%CE%BD_%CF%80%CE%B5%CF%84%CE%B1%CE%BB%CE%BF%CF%8D%CE%B4%CF%89%CE%BD.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%CE%97_%CE%BA%CE%BF%CE%B9%CE%BB%CE%AC%CE%B4%CE%B1_%CF%84%CF%89%CE%BD_%CF%80%CE%B5%CF%84%CE%B1%CE%BB%CE%BF%CF%8D%CE%B4%CF%89%CE%BD.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Valley of
         <a href="/wiki/Petaloudes" title="Petaloudes">
          Petaloudes
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The island of Rhodes is shaped like a
       <a href="/wiki/Spear" title="Spear">
        spearhead
       </a>
       , 79.7 km (49.5 mi) long and 38 km (24 mi) wide, with a total area of approximately 1,400 square kilometres (541 sq mi) and a coastline of approximately 220 km (137 mi).
       <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">
        Limestone
       </a>
       is the main bedrock.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rhodes,_Greece" title="Rhodes, Greece">
        city of Rhodes
       </a>
       is located at the northern tip of the island, as well as the site of the ancient and modern commercial
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Harbour" title="Harbour">
        harbours
       </a>
       . The main air gateway (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diagoras_Airport" title="Diagoras Airport">
        Diagoras International Airport
       </a>
       , IATA code: RHO) is located 14 km (9 mi) to the southwest of the city in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paradisi,_Greece" title="Paradisi, Greece">
        Paradisi
       </a>
       . The road network radiates from the city along the east and west coasts.
      </p>
      <p>
       Outside of the city of Rhodes, the island is dotted with small villages and spa resorts, among them
       <a href="/wiki/Faliraki" title="Faliraki">
        Faliraki
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Lindos" title="Lindos">
        Lindos
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Kremasti" title="Kremasti">
        Kremasti
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haraki" title="Haraki">
        Haraki
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Pefkos" title="Pefkos">
        Pefkos
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Archangelos,_Rhodes" title="Archangelos, Rhodes">
        Archangelos
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Afantou" title="Afantou">
        Afantou
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ixia" title="Ixia">
        Ixia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Koskinou" title="Koskinou">
        Koskinou
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Embona" title="Embona">
        Embona
       </a>
       (Attavyros),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paradisi,_Greece" title="Paradisi, Greece">
        Paradisi
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trianta" title="Trianta">
        Trianta
       </a>
       (Ialysos). There are mineral-rich spring water (and sometimes sea water) used to give medicinal baths and the spa resorts offer various health treatments.
      </p>
      <p>
       Rhodes is situated 363 km (226 mi) east-south-east from the Greek mainland, and 18 km (11 mi) from the southern shore of
       <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">
        Turkey
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Flora">
        Flora
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rhodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Flora">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Natural_history_of_Rhodes" title="Natural history of Rhodes">
        Natural history of Rhodes
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The interior of the island is mountainous, sparsely inhabited and covered with forests of
       <a href="/wiki/Pine" title="Pine">
        pine
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Pinus_brutia" title="Pinus brutia">
         Pinus brutia
        </a>
       </i>
       ) and
       <a href="/wiki/Cupressus_sempervirens" title="Cupressus sempervirens">
        cypress
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        Cupressus sempervirens
       </i>
       ). While the shores are rocky, the island has arable strips of land where
       <a href="/wiki/Citrus" title="Citrus">
        citrus
       </a>
       fruit,
       <a href="/wiki/Wine" title="Wine">
        wine
       </a>
       grapes, vegetables,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Olives" title="Olives">
        olives
       </a>
       and other crops are grown.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Fauna">
        Fauna
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rhodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Fauna">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Natural_history_of_Rhodes" title="Natural history of Rhodes">
        Natural history of Rhodes
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Rhodian population of
       <a href="/wiki/Fallow_deer" title="Fallow deer">
        fallow deer
       </a>
       was found to be genetically distinct in 2005, and to be of urgent conservation concern.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/Petaloudes" title="Petaloudes">
        Petaloudes
       </a>
       Valley (Greek for "Valley of the Butterflies"), large numbers of
       <a href="/wiki/Euplagia_quadripunctaria" title="Euplagia quadripunctaria">
        tiger moths
       </a>
       gather during the summer months. Mount
       <a href="/wiki/Attavyros" title="Attavyros">
        Attavyros
       </a>
       , at 1,216 metres (3,990 ft), is the island's highest point of elevation.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Earthquakes">
        Earthquakes
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rhodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Earthquakes">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Earthquakes include the
       <a href="/wiki/226_BC_Rhodes_earthquake" title="226 BC Rhodes earthquake">
        226 BC earthquake
       </a>
       that destroyed the
       <a href="/wiki/Colossus_of_Rhodes" title="Colossus of Rhodes">
        Colossus of Rhodes
       </a>
       ;
       <a href="/wiki/1481_Rhodes_earthquake" title="1481 Rhodes earthquake">
        one on 3 May 1481
       </a>
       which destroyed much of the city of Rhodes;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and one on 26 June 1926.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On 15 July 2008, Rhodes was struck by a
       <a href="/wiki/2008_Dodecanese_earthquake" title="2008 Dodecanese earthquake">
        6.3 magnitude earthquake
       </a>
       causing minor damage to a few old buildings and one death.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">
        Climate
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rhodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Climate">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Rhodes has a hot-summer
       <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">
        Mediterranean climate
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        Csa
       </i>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">
        Köppen climate classification
       </a>
       ).
      </p>

         26.7
         <br/>
         (80.1)
        </td>
        <td style="background:#FF7900;color:#000000;">
         23.8
         <br/>
         (74.8)
        </td>

         <br/>

        </td>

        </td>

       </tr>

         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weather_Atlas_16-1">

          </a>
         </sup>
