      </table>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rhodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: History">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Early_and_classical_antiquity">
        Early and classical antiquity
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rhodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Early and classical antiquity">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Carnelian_necklace_As_7702.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4078" data-file-width="4618" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Carnelian_necklace_As_7702.jpg/180px-Carnelian_necklace_As_7702.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Carnelian_necklace_As_7702.jpg/270px-Carnelian_necklace_As_7702.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Carnelian_necklace_As_7702.jpg/360px-Carnelian_necklace_As_7702.jpg 2x" width="180"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Carnelian_necklace_As_7702.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Mycenean necklace of carnelian found in
         <a href="/wiki/Kattavia" title="Kattavia">
          Kattavia
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rhodes_88-42_BC-AD.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="350" data-file-width="745" height="103" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Rhodes_88-42_BC-AD.jpg/220px-Rhodes_88-42_BC-AD.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Rhodes_88-42_BC-AD.jpg/330px-Rhodes_88-42_BC-AD.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Rhodes_88-42_BC-AD.jpg/440px-Rhodes_88-42_BC-AD.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rhodes_88-42_BC-AD.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Silver
         <a href="/wiki/Greek_drachma" title="Greek drachma">
          drachma
         </a>
         of Rhodes, 88/42 BC. Obverse: Radiate head of
         <a href="/wiki/Helios" title="Helios">
          Helios
         </a>
         . Reverse:
         <a href="/wiki/Rose" title="Rose">
          Rose
         </a>
         ,
         <i>
          "rhodon"
         </i>
         (ῥόδον) the symbol of Rhodes.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Apollon_temple_acropolis_Rhodes.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4592" data-file-width="3056" height="301" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Apollon_temple_acropolis_Rhodes.jpg/200px-Apollon_temple_acropolis_Rhodes.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Apollon_temple_acropolis_Rhodes.jpg/300px-Apollon_temple_acropolis_Rhodes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Apollon_temple_acropolis_Rhodes.jpg/400px-Apollon_temple_acropolis_Rhodes.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Apollon_temple_acropolis_Rhodes.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Temple of Apollo at the
         <a href="/wiki/Acropolis_of_Rhodes" title="Acropolis of Rhodes">
          Acropolis of Rhodes
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The island was inhabited in the
       <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">
        Neolithic
       </a>
       period, although little remains of this culture. In the 16th century BC, the
       <a href="/wiki/Minoan_civilization" title="Minoan civilization">
        Minoans
       </a>
       came to Rhodes. Later Greek mythology recalled a Rhodian race called the
       <a href="/wiki/Telchines" title="Telchines">
        Telchines
       </a>
       and associated the island of Rhodes with
       <a href="/wiki/Danaus" title="Danaus">
        Danaus
       </a>
       ; it was sometimes nicknamed
       <i>
        Telchinis
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In the 15th century BC,
       <a href="/wiki/Mycenaean_Greece" title="Mycenaean Greece">
        Mycenaean Greeks
       </a>
       invaded. After the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bronze_Age_collapse" title="Bronze Age collapse">
        Bronze Age collapse
       </a>
       , the first renewed outside contacts were with
       <a href="/wiki/Ancient_history_of_Cyprus" title="Ancient history of Cyprus">
        Cyprus
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In the 8th century BC, the island's settlements started to form, with the coming of the
       <a href="/wiki/Dorians" title="Dorians">
        Dorians
       </a>
       , who built the three important cities of Lindos,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ialyssos" title="Ialyssos">
        Ialyssos
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Kameiros" title="Kameiros">
        Kameiros
       </a>
       , which together with
       <a href="/wiki/Kos" title="Kos">
        Kos
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Knidos" title="Knidos">
        Cnidus
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Halicarnassus" title="Halicarnassus">
        Halicarnassus
       </a>
       (on the mainland) made up the so-called
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doric_hexapolis" title="Doric hexapolis">
        Dorian Hexapolis
       </a>
       (Greek for six cities).
      </p>
      <p>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/Pindar" title="Pindar">
        Pindar
       </a>
       's ode, the island was said to be born of the union of
       <a href="/wiki/Helios" title="Helios">
        Helios
       </a>
       the sun god and the nymph
       <a href="/wiki/Rhodos" title="Rhodos">
        Rhodos
       </a>
       , and the cities were named for their three sons. The
       <i>
        rhoda
       </i>
       is a pink
       <a href="/wiki/Hibiscus" title="Hibiscus">
        hibiscus
       </a>
       native to the island.
       <a href="/wiki/Diodorus_Siculus" title="Diodorus Siculus">
        Diodorus Siculus
       </a>
       added that
       <a href="/wiki/Actis" title="Actis">
        Actis
       </a>
       , one of the sons of Helios and Rhode, travelled to
       <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">
        Egypt
       </a>
       . He built the city of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heliopolis_(Ancient_Egypt)" title="Heliopolis (Ancient Egypt)">
        Heliopolis
       </a>
       and taught the Egyptians
       <a href="/wiki/Astrology" title="Astrology">
        astrology
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
        <a href="#cite_note-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Homer" title="Homer">
        Homer
       </a>
       mentions that Rhodes participated in the
       <a href="/wiki/Trojan_War" title="Trojan War">
        Trojan War
       </a>
       under the leadership of
       <a href="/wiki/Tlepolemus" title="Tlepolemus">
        Tlepolemus
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In the second half of the 8th century, the sanctuary of Athena received votive gifts that are markers for cultural contacts: small ivories from the Near East and bronze objects from Syria. At
       <a href="/wiki/Kameiros" title="Kameiros">
        Kameiros
       </a>
       on the northwest coast, a former Bronze Age site, where the temple was founded in the 8th century, there is another notable contemporaneous sequence of carved ivory figurines. The cemeteries of Kameiros and Ialyssos yielded several exquisite exemplars of the Orientalizing Rhodian jewellery, dated in the 7th and early 6th centuries BC.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Phoenician presence on the island at
       <a href="/wiki/Ialysos" title="Ialysos">
        Ialysos
       </a>
       is attested in traditions recorded much later by Rhodian historians.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2012)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">
        Persians
       </a>
       invaded and overran the island, but they were in turn defeated by forces from
       <a href="/wiki/Classical_Athens" title="Classical Athens">
        Athens
       </a>
       in 478 BC. The Rhodian cities joined the
       <a href="/wiki/Delian_League" title="Delian League">
        Athenian League
       </a>
       . When the
       <a href="/wiki/Peloponnesian_War" title="Peloponnesian War">
        Peloponnesian War
       </a>
       broke out in 431 BC, Rhodes remained largely neutral, although it remained a member of the League. The war lasted until 404 BC, but by this time Rhodes had withdrawn entirely from the conflict and decided to go her own way.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2012)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 408 BC, the cities
       <a href="/wiki/Synoecism" title="Synoecism">
        united to form one territory
       </a>
       . They built the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/City_of_Rhodes" title="City of Rhodes">
        city of Rhodes
       </a>
       , a new capital on the northern end of the island. Its regular plan was, according to
       <a href="/wiki/Strabo" title="Strabo">
        Strabo
       </a>
       , superintended by the Athenian architect
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hippodamus" title="Hippodamus">
        Hippodamus
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In 357 BC, the island was conquered by the king
       <a href="/wiki/Mausolus" title="Mausolus">
        Mausolus
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Caria" title="Caria">
        Caria
       </a>
       , then it fell again to the Persians in 340 BC. Their rule was also short.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Hellenistic_age">
        Hellenistic age
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rhodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Hellenistic age">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Rhodes then became a part of the growing empire of
       <a href="/wiki/Alexander_the_Great" title="Alexander the Great">
        Alexander the Great
       </a>
       in 332 BC, after he defeated the Persians.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2012)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Colosse_de_Rhodes_(Barclay).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="900" data-file-width="600" height="270" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Colosse_de_Rhodes_%28Barclay%29.jpg/180px-Colosse_de_Rhodes_%28Barclay%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Colosse_de_Rhodes_%28Barclay%29.jpg/270px-Colosse_de_Rhodes_%28Barclay%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Colosse_de_Rhodes_%28Barclay%29.jpg/360px-Colosse_de_Rhodes_%28Barclay%29.jpg 2x" width="180"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Colosse_de_Rhodes_(Barclay).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Colossus_of_Rhodes" title="Colossus of Rhodes">
          Colossus of Rhodes
         </a>
         , as depicted in an artist's impression of 1880.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Following the death of Alexander,
       <a href="/wiki/Diadochi" title="Diadochi">
        his generals
       </a>
       vied for control of the kingdom. Three—
       <a href="/wiki/Ptolemy_I_Soter" title="Ptolemy I Soter">
        Ptolemy
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Seleucus_I_Nicator" title="Seleucus I Nicator">
        Seleucus
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Antigonus_I_Monophthalmus" title="Antigonus I Monophthalmus">
        Antigonus
       </a>
       —succeeded in dividing the kingdom among themselves. Rhodes formed strong commercial and cultural ties
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       with the Ptolemies in
       <a href="/wiki/Alexandria" title="Alexandria">
        Alexandria
       </a>
       , and together formed the Rhodo-Egyptian alliance that controlled trade throughout the Aegean in the 3rd century BC.
      </p>
      <p>
       The city developed into a maritime, commercial and cultural center; its coins circulated nearly everywhere in the Mediterranean. Its famous schools of philosophy, science, literature and
       <a href="/wiki/Rhetoric" title="Rhetoric">
        rhetoric
       </a>
       shared masters with Alexandria: the Athenian rhetorician
       <a href="/wiki/Aeschines" title="Aeschines">
        Aeschines
       </a>
       , who formed a school at Rhodes;
       <a href="/wiki/Apollonius_of_Rhodes" title="Apollonius of Rhodes">
        Apollonius of Rhodes
       </a>
       ;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the observations and works of the astronomers
       <a href="/wiki/Hipparchus" title="Hipparchus">
        Hipparchus
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Geminus" title="Geminus">
        Geminus
       </a>
       , the rhetorician
       <a href="/wiki/Dionysius_Thrax" title="Dionysius Thrax">
        Dionysius Thrax
       </a>
       . Its school of sculptors developed, under
       <a href="/wiki/Pergamon" title="Pergamon">
        Pergamese
       </a>
       influence, a rich, dramatic style that can be characterized as "
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hellenistic_civilization" title="Hellenistic civilization">
        Hellenistic
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Baroque" title="Baroque">
        Baroque
       </a>
       ".
       <a href="/wiki/Agesander_of_Rhodes" title="Agesander of Rhodes">
        Agesander of Rhodes
       </a>
       , with two other Rhodian sculptors, carved the famous
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Laoco%C3%B6n_and_His_Sons" title="Laocoön and His Sons">
         Laocoön group
        </a>
       </i>
       , now in the
       <a href="/wiki/Vatican_Museums" title="Vatican Museums">
        Vatican Museums
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/Sperlonga_sculptures" title="Sperlonga sculptures">
        large sculptures rediscovered at Sperlonga
       </a>
       in the villa of
       <a href="/wiki/Tiberius" title="Tiberius">
        Tiberius
       </a>
       , probably in the early
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">
        Imperial period
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 305 BC, Antigonus directed his son,
       <a href="/wiki/Demetrius_I_of_Macedon" title="Demetrius I of Macedon">
        Demetrius
       </a>
       , to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siege_of_Rhodes_(305_BC)" title="Siege of Rhodes (305 BC)">
        besiege Rhodes
       </a>
       in an attempt to break its alliance with Egypt. Demetrius created huge
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siege_engines" title="Siege engines">
        siege engines
       </a>
       , including a 180 ft (55 m)
       <a href="/wiki/Battering_ram" title="Battering ram">
        battering ram
       </a>
       and a
       <a href="/wiki/Siege_tower" title="Siege tower">
        siege tower
       </a>
       named
       <a href="/wiki/Helepolis" title="Helepolis">
        Helepolis
       </a>
       that weighed 360,000 pounds (163,293 kg). Despite this engagement, in 304 BC after only one year, he relented and signed a peace agreement, leaving behind a huge store of military equipment. The Rhodians sold the equipment and used the money to erect a statue of their sun god,
       <a href="/wiki/Helios" title="Helios">
        Helios
       </a>
       , the statue since called the
       <a href="/wiki/Colossus_of_Rhodes" title="Colossus of Rhodes">
        Colossus of Rhodes
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2012)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Throughout the 3rd century BC, Rhodes attempted to secure her independence and her commerce, most especially her virtual control over the grain trade in the eastern Mediterranean. Both of these goals were dependent upon no one of the three great Hellenistic states achieving dominance, and consequently the Rhodians pursued a policy of maintaining a balance of power among the Antigonids, Seleucids and Ptolemies, even if that meant going to war with her traditional ally, Egypt. To this end they employed as leverage their economy and their excellent navy, which was manned by proverbially the finest sailors in the Mediterranean world: "If we have ten Rhodians, we have ten ships."
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2012)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       The Rhodians also established their dominance on the shores of
       <a href="/wiki/Caria" title="Caria">
        Caria
       </a>
       across their island, which became known as the "
       <a href="/wiki/Rhodian_Peraia" title="Rhodian Peraia">
        Rhodian Peraia
       </a>
       ". It extended roughly from the modern city of
       <a href="/wiki/Mu%C4%9Fla" title="Muğla">
        Muğla
       </a>
       (ancient
       <i>
        Mobolla
       </i>
       ) in the north and
       <a href="/wiki/Kaunos" title="Kaunos">
        Kaunos
       </a>
       bordering
       <a href="/wiki/Lycia" title="Lycia">
        Lycia
       </a>
       in the south, near the present-day
       <a href="/wiki/Dalyan" title="Dalyan">
        Dalyan
       </a>
       , Turkey.
      </p>
      <p>
       Rhodes successfully carried on this policy through the course of the third century BC, an impressive achievement for what was essentially a democratic state. By the end of that period, however, the balance of power was crumbling, as declining Ptolemaic power made Egypt an attractive target for Seleucid ambitions. In 203/2 BC the young and dynamic kings of Antigonid Macedon and Seleucid Asia,
       <a href="/wiki/Philip_V_of_Macedon" title="Philip V of Macedon">
        Philip V
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antiochus_III" title="Antiochus III">
        Antiochus III
       </a>
       , agreed to accept—at least temporarily—their respective military ambitions, Philip's campaign in the Aegean and western Anatolia and Antiochus’ final solution of the Egyptian question. Heading a coalition of small states, the Rhodians
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Chios_(201_BC)" title="Battle of Chios (201 BC)">
        checked Philip's navy
       </a>
       , but not his superior army. Without a third power to which to turn, the Rhodians appealed in 201 BC to the
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Republic" title="Roman Republic">
        Roman Republic
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2012)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rhodos_Ritterkastell_bei_Lindos.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2560" data-file-width="1920" height="240" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Rhodos_Ritterkastell_bei_Lindos.jpg/180px-Rhodos_Ritterkastell_bei_Lindos.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Rhodos_Ritterkastell_bei_Lindos.jpg/270px-Rhodos_Ritterkastell_bei_Lindos.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Rhodos_Ritterkastell_bei_Lindos.jpg/360px-Rhodos_Ritterkastell_bei_Lindos.jpg 2x" width="180"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rhodos_Ritterkastell_bei_Lindos.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Medieval gate at the Acropolis of
         <a href="/wiki/Lindos" title="Lindos">
          Lindos
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Despite being exhausted by the
       <a href="/wiki/Second_Punic_War" title="Second Punic War">
        titanic struggle
       </a>
       against
       <a href="/wiki/Hannibal" title="Hannibal">
        Hannibal
       </a>
       (218-201 BC) the Romans agreed to intervene, having already been
       <a href="/wiki/First_Macedonian_War" title="First Macedonian War">
        stabbed in the back
       </a>
       by Philip during the war against Carthage. The Senate saw the appeal from Rhodes and her allies as the opportunity to pressure Philip. The result was the
       <a href="/wiki/Second_Macedonian_War" title="Second Macedonian War">
        Second Macedonian War
       </a>
       (200-196 BC), which ended Macedon's role as a major player and preserved Rhodian independence.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2012)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Rhodian influence in the Aegean was cemented through the organization of the
       <a href="/wiki/Cyclades" title="Cyclades">
        Cyclades
       </a>
       into the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_Nesiotic_League" title="Second Nesiotic League">
        Second Nesiotic League
       </a>
       under Rhodian leadership.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Romans actually withdrew from Greece after the end of the conflict, but the resulting power vacuum quickly drew in Antiochus and subsequently the Romans, who
       <a href="/wiki/Roman%E2%80%93Seleucid_War" title="Roman–Seleucid War">
        defeated
       </a>
       (192-188 BC) the last Mediterranean power that might even vaguely threaten their predominance. Having provided Rome with valuable naval help in her first foray into Asia, the Rhodians were rewarded with territory and enhanced status.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2012)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       The Romans once again evacuated the east – the Senate preferred clients to provinces – but it was clear that Rome now ruled the world and Rhodian autonomy was ultimately dependent upon good relations with them.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2012)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       And those good graces soon evaporated in the wake of the
       <a href="/wiki/Third_Macedonian_War" title="Third Macedonian War">
        Third Macedonian War
       </a>
       (171-168 BC). In 169 BC, during the war against
       <a href="/wiki/Perseus_of_Macedon" title="Perseus of Macedon">
        Perseus
       </a>
       , Rhodes sent
       <a href="/wiki/Agepolis" title="Agepolis">
        Agepolis
       </a>
       as ambassador to the consul
       <a href="/wiki/Quintus_Marcius_Philippus_(consul_186_BC)" title="Quintus Marcius Philippus (consul 186 BC)">
        Quintus Marcius Philippus
       </a>
       , and then to Rome in the following year, hoping to turn the Senate against the war.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Rhodes remained scrupulously neutral during the war, but in the view of hostile elements in the Senate she had been a bit too friendly with the defeated King Perseus. Some actually proposed declaring war on the island republic, but this was averted. In 164, Rhodes became a permanent ally of Rome, ending an independence that no longer had any meaning.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">
          <span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (June 2012)">
           clarification needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       It was said that the Romans ultimately turned against the Rhodians because the islanders were the only people they had encountered who were more arrogant than themselves.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2012)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       After surrendering its independence Rhodes became a cultural and educational center for Roman noble families and was especially noted for its teachers of rhetoric, such as
       <a href="/wiki/Hermagoras_of_Temnos" title="Hermagoras of Temnos">
        Hermagoras
       </a>
       and the unknown author of
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Rhetorica_ad_Herennium" title="Rhetorica ad Herennium">
         Rhetorica ad Herennium
        </a>
       </i>
       . At first, the state was an important ally of Rome and enjoyed numerous privileges, but these were later lost in various machinations of Roman politics.
       <a href="/wiki/Gaius_Cassius_Longinus" title="Gaius Cassius Longinus">
        Cassius
       </a>
       eventually invaded the island and sacked the city. In the early Imperial period Rhodes became a favorite place for political exiles.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In the 1st century AD, the Emperor
       <a href="/wiki/Tiberius" title="Tiberius">
        Tiberius
       </a>
       spent a brief term of exile on Rhodes.
       <a href="/wiki/Paul_the_Apostle" title="Paul the Apostle">
        Saint Paul
       </a>
       brought
       <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">
        Christianity
       </a>
       to people on the island.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Rhodes reached her zenith in the 3rd century.
      </p>
      <p>
       In ancient times there was a Roman saying: "
       <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/hic_Rhodus,_hic_salta" title="wiktionary:hic Rhodus, hic salta">
        hic Rhodus, hic salta
       </a>
       !"—"Here is Rhodes, jump here", an admonition to prove one's idle boasts by deed rather than talk. It comes from an
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aesop%27s_fable" title="Aesop's fable">
        Aesop's fable
       </a>
       called "The Boastful Athlete" and was cited by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hegel" title="Hegel">
        Hegel
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marx" title="Marx">
        Marx
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Byzantine_period">
        Byzantine period
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rhodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Byzantine period">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In 395 with the division of the
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">
        Roman Empire
       </a>
       , the long
       <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">
        Byzantine
       </a>
       period began for Rhodes. In
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Late_Antiquity" title="Late Antiquity">
        Late Antiquity
       </a>
       , the island was the capital of the
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_province" title="Roman province">
        Roman province
       </a>
       of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Islands_(Roman_province)" title="Islands (Roman province)">
        Islands
       </a>
       , headed by a
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Praeses" title="Praeses">
         praeses
        </a>
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hegemon" title="Hegemon">
         hegemon
        </a>
       </i>
       in Greek), and encompassing most of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aegean_islands" title="Aegean islands">
        Aegean islands
       </a>
       , with twenty cities. Correspondingly, the island was also the
       <a href="/wiki/Metropolis_of_Rhodes" title="Metropolis of Rhodes">
        metropolis
       </a>
       of the ecclesiastical province of Cyclades, with eleven
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suffragan" title="Suffragan">
        suffragan
       </a>
       sees.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODB_27-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ODB-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Beginning from ca. 600 AD, its influence in maritime issues was manifested in the collection of
       <a href="/wiki/Admiralty_law" title="Admiralty law">
        maritime laws
       </a>
       known as "
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rhodian_Sea_Law" title="Rhodian Sea Law">
        Rhodian Sea Law
       </a>
       " (
       <i>
        Nomos Rhodion Nautikos
       </i>
       ), accepted throughout the Mediterranean and in use throughout Byzantine times (and influencing the development of
       <a href="/wiki/Admiralty_law#History_of_admiralty_law" title="Admiralty law">
        admiralty law
       </a>
       up to the present).
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="'up to the present' needs some kind of footnote (April 2011)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       In 622/3, during the climactic
       <a href="/wiki/Byzantine%E2%80%93Sasanian_War_of_602%E2%80%93628" title="Byzantine–Sasanian War of 602–628">
        Byzantine–Sasanian War of 602–628
       </a>
       , Rhodes was captured by the
       <a href="/wiki/Sasanian_navy" title="Sasanian navy">
        Sasanian navy
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKia2016223_28-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKia2016223-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGreatrexLieu2005197_29-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGreatrexLieu2005197-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoward-Johnston200633_30-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoward-Johnston200633-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Rhodes was occupied by the Islamic
       <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_Caliphate" title="Umayyad Caliphate">
        Umayyad
       </a>
       forces of Caliph
       <a href="/wiki/Muawiyah_I" title="Muawiyah I">
        Muawiyah I
       </a>
       in 654, who carried off the remains of the Colossus of Rhodes.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODB_27-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-ODB-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The island was again captured by the Arabs in 673 as part of their
       <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Constantinople_(674%E2%80%93678)" title="Siege of Constantinople (674–678)">
        first attack on Constantinople
       </a>
       . When their fleet was destroyed by
       <a href="/wiki/Greek_fire" title="Greek fire">
        Greek fire
       </a>
       before Constantinople and by storms on its return trip, however, the island was evacuated in 679/80 as part of the Byzantine–Umayyad peace treaty.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 715 the Byzantine fleet dispatched against the Arabs launched a rebellion at Rhodes, which led to the installation of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Theodosios_III" title="Theodosios III">
        Theodosios III
       </a>
       on the Byzantine throne.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODB_27-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-ODB-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       From the early 8th to the 12th centuries, Rhodes belonged to the
       <a href="/wiki/Cibyrrhaeot_Theme" title="Cibyrrhaeot Theme">
        Cibyrrhaeot Theme
       </a>
       of the Byzantine Empire, and was a centre for shipbuilding and commerce.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODB_27-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-ODB-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In
       <abbr title="circa">
        c.
       </abbr>
       1090, it was occupied by the forces of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seljuk_dynasty" title="Seljuk dynasty">
        Seljuk Turks
       </a>
       , not long after the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Manzikert" title="Battle of Manzikert">
        Battle of Manzikert
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Rhodes was recaptured by the Emperor
       <a href="/wiki/Alexios_I_Komnenos" title="Alexios I Komnenos">
        Alexios I Komnenos
       </a>
       during the
       <a href="/wiki/First_Crusade" title="First Crusade">
        First Crusade
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rhodes-TerrePleinSpain.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1060" data-file-width="1600" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Rhodes-TerrePleinSpain.JPG/220px-Rhodes-TerrePleinSpain.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Rhodes-TerrePleinSpain.JPG/330px-Rhodes-TerrePleinSpain.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Rhodes-TerrePleinSpain.JPG/440px-Rhodes-TerrePleinSpain.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rhodes-TerrePleinSpain.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Part of the late medieval
         <a href="/wiki/Fortifications_of_Rhodes" title="Fortifications of Rhodes">
          Fortifications of Rhodes
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       As Byzantine central power weakened under the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Angeloi" title="Angeloi">
        Angeloi
       </a>
       emperors (1185–1204), in the first half of the 13th century, Rhodes became the centre of an independent domain under
       <a href="/wiki/Leo_Gabalas" title="Leo Gabalas">
        Leo Gabalas
       </a>
       and his brother
       <a href="/wiki/John_Gabalas" title="John Gabalas">
        John
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODB_27-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-ODB-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       until it was
       <a href="/wiki/Genoese_occupation_of_Rhodes" title="Genoese occupation of Rhodes">
        occupied
       </a>
       by the
       <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Genoa" title="Republic of Genoa">
        Genoese
       </a>
       in 1248–1250. The Genoese were evicted by the
       <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Nicaea" title="Empire of Nicaea">
        Empire of Nicaea
       </a>
       , after which the island became a regular province of the Nicaean state (and after 1261 of the restored Byzantine Empire). In 1305, the island was given as a fief to
       <a href="/wiki/Andrea_Morisco" title="Andrea Morisco">
        Andrea Morisco
       </a>
       , a Genoese adventurer who had entered Byzantine service. But, Rhodes was controlled by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mente%C5%9Fe_(beylik)" title="Menteşe (beylik)">
        Menteşe
       </a>
       , was one of Anatolian beyliks between 1300 and 1314.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Crusader_and_Islamic_rule">
        Crusader and Islamic rule
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rhodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Crusader and Islamic rule">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Knights_Hospitaller" title="Knights Hospitaller">
        Knights Hospitaller
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:OttomanJanissariesAndDefendingKnightsOfStJohnSiegeOfRhodes1522.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1052" data-file-width="1046" height="181" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/OttomanJanissariesAndDefendingKnightsOfStJohnSiegeOfRhodes1522.jpg/180px-OttomanJanissariesAndDefendingKnightsOfStJohnSiegeOfRhodes1522.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/OttomanJanissariesAndDefendingKnightsOfStJohnSiegeOfRhodes1522.jpg/270px-OttomanJanissariesAndDefendingKnightsOfStJohnSiegeOfRhodes1522.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/OttomanJanissariesAndDefendingKnightsOfStJohnSiegeOfRhodes1522.jpg/360px-OttomanJanissariesAndDefendingKnightsOfStJohnSiegeOfRhodes1522.jpg 2x" width="180"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:OttomanJanissariesAndDefendingKnightsOfStJohnSiegeOfRhodes1522.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Ottoman
         <a href="/wiki/Janissaries" title="Janissaries">
          Janissaries
         </a>
         and defending
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Knights_of_Saint_John" title="Knights of Saint John">
          Knights of Saint John
         </a>
         at the
         <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Rhodes_(1522)" title="Siege of Rhodes (1522)">
          Siege of Rhodes
         </a>
         in 1522, from an Ottoman manuscript.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A_small_harbour_in_Rhodes.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2183" data-file-width="3288" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/A_small_harbour_in_Rhodes.jpg/220px-A_small_harbour_in_Rhodes.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/A_small_harbour_in_Rhodes.jpg/330px-A_small_harbour_in_Rhodes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/A_small_harbour_in_Rhodes.jpg/440px-A_small_harbour_in_Rhodes.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:A_small_harbour_in_Rhodes.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Rhodes in the 19th century
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 1306–1310, the Byzantine era of the island's history came to an end when
       <a href="/wiki/Hospitaller_conquest_of_Rhodes" title="Hospitaller conquest of Rhodes">
        the island was occupied
       </a>
       by the
       <a href="/wiki/Knights_Hospitaller" title="Knights Hospitaller">
        Knights Hospitaller
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODB_27-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-ODB-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Under the rule of the newly named "Knights of Rhodes", the city was rebuilt into a model of the European medieval ideal. Many of the city's famous monuments, including the
       <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_the_Grand_Master_of_the_Knights_of_Rhodes" title="Palace of the Grand Master of the Knights of Rhodes">
        Palace of the Grand Master
       </a>
       , were built during this period.
      </p>
      <p>
       The strong walls which the knights had built withstood the attacks of the
       <a href="/wiki/Sultan_of_Egypt" title="Sultan of Egypt">
        Sultan of Egypt
       </a>
       in 1444, and a
       <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Rhodes_(1480)" title="Siege of Rhodes (1480)">
        siege
       </a>
       by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ottomans" title="Ottomans">
        Ottomans
       </a>
       under
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mehmed_II" title="Mehmed II">
        Mehmed II
       </a>
       in 1480. Eventually, however, Rhodes
       <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Rhodes_(1522)" title="Siege of Rhodes (1522)">
        fell
       </a>
       to the large army of
       <a href="/wiki/Suleiman_the_Magnificent" title="Suleiman the Magnificent">
        Suleiman the Magnificent
       </a>
       in December 1522. The Sultan deployed 400 ships delivering 100,000 men to the island (200,000 in other sources). Against this force the Knights, under Grand Master
       <a href="/wiki/Philippe_Villiers_de_L%27Isle-Adam" title="Philippe Villiers de L'Isle-Adam">
        Philippe Villiers de L'Isle-Adam
       </a>
       , had about 7,000 men-at-arms and their fortifications. The siege lasted six months, at the end of which the surviving defeated Hospitallers were allowed to withdraw to the
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Sicily" title="Kingdom of Sicily">
        Kingdom of Sicily
       </a>
       . Despite the defeat, both Christians and Muslims seem to have regarded the conduct of Villiers de L'Isle-Adam as extremely valiant, and the Grand Master was proclaimed a Defender of the Faith by Pope Adrian VI (see
       <a href="/wiki/Knights_Hospitaller#Knights_of_Cyprus_and_Rhodes" title="Knights Hospitaller">
        Knights of Cyprus and Rhodes
       </a>
       ). The knights would later move their base of operations to
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Malta_under_the_Order_of_Saint_John" title="History of Malta under the Order of Saint John">
        Malta
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Rhodes was thereafter a possession of the
       <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">
        Ottoman Empire
       </a>
       (see
       <a href="/wiki/Sanjak_of_Rhodes" title="Sanjak of Rhodes">
        Sanjak of Rhodes
       </a>
       ) for nearly four centuries.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_history">
        Modern history
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rhodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Modern history">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rhodus_type_M%C3%BCller_A86.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="429" data-file-width="371" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Rhodus_type_M%C3%BCller_A86.jpg/120px-Rhodus_type_M%C3%BCller_A86.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Rhodus_type_M%C3%BCller_A86.jpg/180px-Rhodus_type_M%C3%BCller_A86.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Rhodus_type_M%C3%BCller_A86.jpg/240px-Rhodus_type_M%C3%BCller_A86.jpg 2x" width="120"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rhodus_type_M%C3%BCller_A86.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         5 soldi Austrian Levant stamp cancelled in brown
         <i>
          RHODUS
         </i>
         .
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
          <a href="#cite_note-35">
           [35]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Offices_of_the_Prefecture_of_the_Dodecanese_02.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2434" data-file-width="3456" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Offices_of_the_Prefecture_of_the_Dodecanese_02.jpg/220px-Offices_of_the_Prefecture_of_the_Dodecanese_02.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Offices_of_the_Prefecture_of_the_Dodecanese_02.jpg/330px-Offices_of_the_Prefecture_of_the_Dodecanese_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Offices_of_the_Prefecture_of_the_Dodecanese_02.jpg/440px-Offices_of_the_Prefecture_of_the_Dodecanese_02.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Offices_of_the_Prefecture_of_the_Dodecanese_02.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <i>
          Palazzo Governale
         </i>
         (today the offices of the Prefecture of the Dodecanese), built during the Italian period.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The island was populated by ethnic groups from the surrounding nations, including Jews. Under Ottoman rule, they generally did fairly well, but discrimination and bigotry occasionally arose. In February 1840, the Jews of Rhodes were falsely accused of ritually murdering a Christian boy. This became known as the
       <a href="/wiki/Rhodes_blood_libel" title="Rhodes blood libel">
        Rhodes blood libel
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Austria opened a post-office at
       <i>
        RHODUS
       </i>
       (Venetian name) before 1864,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
        <a href="#cite_note-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
       as witnessed by stamps with Franz-Josef head.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1912, Italy seized Rhodes from the Turks during the
       <a href="/wiki/Italo-Turkish_War" title="Italo-Turkish War">
        Italo-Turkish War
       </a>
       . The island's population thus bypassed many of the events associated with the
       <a href="/wiki/Population_exchange_between_Greece_and_Turkey" title="Population exchange between Greece and Turkey">
        "exchange of the minorities"
       </a>
       between Greece and
       <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">
        Turkey
       </a>
       . After
       <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">
        World War I
       </a>
       , the island, together with the rest of the
       <a href="/wiki/Dodecanese" title="Dodecanese">
        Dodecanese
       </a>
       , was officially assigned to Italy in the
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Lausanne" title="Treaty of Lausanne">
        Treaty of Lausanne
       </a>
       . It then became the core of their possession of the
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Isole_Italiane_dell%27Egeo" title="Isole Italiane dell'Egeo">
         Isole Italiane dell'Egeo
        </a>
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Rhodes harbor 2017:
      </p>
      <div class="center">
       <div class="floatnone">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rhodes_D81_3478_(37745913995).jpg" title="Rhodos hamn 2017">
         <img alt="Rhodos hamn 2017" data-file-height="2445" data-file-width="7335" height="267" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Rhodes_D81_3478_%2837745913995%29.jpg/800px-Rhodes_D81_3478_%2837745913995%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Rhodes_D81_3478_%2837745913995%29.jpg/1200px-Rhodes_D81_3478_%2837745913995%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Rhodes_D81_3478_%2837745913995%29.jpg/1600px-Rhodes_D81_3478_%2837745913995%29.jpg 2x" width="800"/>
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Rhodes panorama 2017:
      </p>
      <div class="center">
       <div class="floatnone">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rhodes_D81_3370_(37746014135).jpg" title="Panorama över Rhodos 2017">
         <img alt="Panorama över Rhodos 2017" data-file-height="4401" data-file-width="15923" height="221" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Rhodes_D81_3370_%2837746014135%29.jpg/800px-Rhodes_D81_3370_%2837746014135%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Rhodes_D81_3370_%2837746014135%29.jpg/1200px-Rhodes_D81_3370_%2837746014135%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Rhodes_D81_3370_%2837746014135%29.jpg/1600px-Rhodes_D81_3370_%2837746014135%29.jpg 2x" width="800"/>
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Following the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Armistice_between_Italy_and_Allied_armed_forces" title="Armistice between Italy and Allied armed forces">
        Italian Armistice of 8 September 1943
       </a>
       , the British attempted to get the Italian garrison on Rhodes to change sides. This was anticipated by the
       <a href="/wiki/German_Army_(Wehrmacht)" title="German Army (Wehrmacht)">
        German Army
       </a>
       , which succeeded in occupying the island with the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Rhodes_(1943)" title="Battle of Rhodes (1943)">
        Battle of Rhodes
       </a>
       . In great measure, the German occupation caused the British failure in the subsequent
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dodecanese_Campaign" title="Dodecanese Campaign">
        Dodecanese Campaign
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">
        Turkish
       </a>
       Consul
       <a href="/wiki/Selahattin_%C3%9Clk%C3%BCmen" title="Selahattin Ülkümen">
        Selahattin Ülkümen
       </a>
       succeeded, at considerable risk to himself and his family, in saving 42 Jewish families, about 200 persons in total, who had Turkish citizenship or were members of Turkish citizens' families.
      </p>
      <p>
       On 8 May 1945 the Germans under
       <a href="/wiki/Otto_Wagener" title="Otto Wagener">
        Otto Wagener
       </a>
       surrendered Rhodes as well as the Dodecanese as a whole to the British, who soon after then occupied the islands as a military protectorate.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1947, Rhodes, together with the other islands of the
       <a href="/wiki/Dodecanese" title="Dodecanese">
        Dodecanese
       </a>
       , was united with Greece.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1949, Rhodes was the venue for negotiations between
       <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">
        Israel
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">
        Egypt
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">
        Jordan
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">
        Lebanon
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">
        Syria
       </a>
       , concluding with the
       <a href="/wiki/1949_Armistice_Agreements" title="1949 Armistice Agreements">
        1949 Armistice Agreements
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The name of the US state of
       <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island" title="Rhode Island">
        Rhode Island
       </a>
       is based on a reference to Rhodes by Italian explorer
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Giovanni_Verrazano" title="Giovanni Verrazano">
        Giovanni Verrazano
       </a>
       . In a 1524 letter detailing his excursion into the waters around either
       <a href="/wiki/Block_Island" title="Block Island">
        Block Island
       </a>
       or
       <a href="/wiki/Aquidneck_Island" title="Aquidneck Island">
        Aquidneck Island
       </a>
       Verrazano wrote that he "discovered an Ilande in the form of a triangle, distant from the maine lande 3 leagues, about the bignesse of the Ilande of the Rodes".
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Archaeology">
        Archaeology
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rhodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Archaeology">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kameiros_-_Fountain_square_03.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2529" data-file-width="3407" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Kameiros_-_Fountain_square_03.jpg/220px-Kameiros_-_Fountain_square_03.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Kameiros_-_Fountain_square_03.jpg/330px-Kameiros_-_Fountain_square_03.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Kameiros_-_Fountain_square_03.jpg/440px-Kameiros_-_Fountain_square_03.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kameiros_-_Fountain_square_03.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Fountain square at the ancient site of
         <a href="/wiki/Kameiros" title="Kameiros">
          Kameiros
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rhodos_Monolithos_R02.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2475" data-file-width="3820" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Rhodos_Monolithos_R02.jpg/220px-Rhodos_Monolithos_R02.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Rhodos_Monolithos_R02.jpg/330px-Rhodos_Monolithos_R02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Rhodos_Monolithos_R02.jpg/440px-Rhodos_Monolithos_R02.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rhodos_Monolithos_R02.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Medieval castle of
         <a href="/wiki/Monolithos,_Greece" title="Monolithos, Greece">
          Monolithos
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Colossus_of_Rhodes" title="Colossus of Rhodes">
        Colossus of Rhodes
       </a>
       was considered to be one of the
       <a href="/wiki/Seven_Wonders_of_the_Ancient_World" title="Seven Wonders of the Ancient World">
        Seven Wonders of the Ancient World
       </a>
       . This giant bronze statue was documented as once standing at the harbour. It was completed in 280 BC and destroyed in an
       <a href="/wiki/Earthquake" title="Earthquake">
        earthquake
       </a>
       in 224 BC. No trace of the statue remains today.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Historical" title="Historical">
        Historical
       </a>
       sites on the island of Rhodes include the
       <a href="/wiki/Lindos" title="Lindos">
        Acropolis of Lindos
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Acropolis_of_Rhodes" title="Acropolis of Rhodes">
        Acropolis of Rhodes
       </a>
       with the Temple of Pythian Apollo and an ancient theatre and stadium,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
        <a href="#cite_note-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       ancient
       <a href="/wiki/Ialysos" title="Ialysos">
        Ialysos
       </a>
       , ancient
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kamiros" title="Kamiros">
        Kamiros
       </a>
       , the
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Governor%27s_Palace_on_Rhodes&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Governor's Palace on Rhodes (page does not exist)">
        Governor's Palace
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Fortifications_of_Rhodes" title="Fortifications of Rhodes">
        Rhodes Old Town
       </a>
       (walled medieval city), the
       <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_the_Grand_Master_of_the_Knights_of_Rhodes" title="Palace of the Grand Master of the Knights of Rhodes">
        Palace of the Grand Masters
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Kahal_Shalom_Synagogue" title="Kahal Shalom Synagogue">
        Kahal Shalom Synagogue
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/La_Juderia" title="La Juderia">
        Jewish Quarter
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Archaeological_Museum_of_Rhodes" title="Archaeological Museum of Rhodes">
        Archeological Museum
       </a>
       , the ruins of the
       <a href="/wiki/Monolithos,_Greece" title="Monolithos, Greece">
        castle of Monolithos
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Kritinia" title="Kritinia">
        castle of Kritinia
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=St._Catherine_Hospice&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="St. Catherine Hospice (page does not exist)">
        St. Catherine Hospice
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Rhodes_Footbridge" title="Rhodes Footbridge">
        Rhodes Footbridge
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">
        Religion
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rhodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Religion">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rhodes_Filerimos3_tango7174.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="840" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Rhodes_Filerimos3_tango7174.jpg/220px-Rhodes_Filerimos3_tango7174.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Rhodes_Filerimos3_tango7174.jpg/330px-Rhodes_Filerimos3_tango7174.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Rhodes_Filerimos3_tango7174.jpg/440px-Rhodes_Filerimos3_tango7174.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rhodes_Filerimos3_tango7174.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Filerimos Monastery in
         <a href="/wiki/Ialysos" title="Ialysos">
          Ialysos
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Christianity">
        Christianity
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rhodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Christianity">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The predominant religion is
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greek_Orthodox" title="Greek Orthodox">
        Greek Orthodox
       </a>
       ; the island is the seat of the
       <a href="/wiki/Metropolis_of_Rhodes" title="Metropolis of Rhodes">
        Metropolis of Rhodes
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       There is a significant
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" title="Roman Catholic Church">
        Latin Catholic
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
        <a href="#cite_note-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       minority on the island, many of whom are descendants of Italians who remained after the end of the Italian occupation, pastorally served by the
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Rhodes" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Rhodes">
        Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Rhodes
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Islam">
        Islam
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rhodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Islam">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Turks_of_the_Dodecanese" title="Turks of the Dodecanese">
        Turks of the Dodecanese
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Rhodes has a
       <a href="/wiki/Turkish_people" title="Turkish people">
        Turkish
       </a>
       Muslim minority, a remnant from
       <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">
        Ottoman Turkish
       </a>
       times. They are organized around the Turkish Association of Rhodes (
       <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">
        Turkish
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="tr" xml:lang="tr">
         Rodos Türk Derneği
        </span>
       </i>
       ), which gives the figure 3,500 for the population they bring together and represent for the island.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
        <a href="#cite_note-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The number of the Turks in Rhodes could be as many as 4,000.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
        <a href="#cite_note-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
        <a href="#cite_note-41">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
        <a href="#cite_note-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Judaism">
        Judaism
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rhodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Judaism">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Selahattin_%C3%9Clk%C3%BCmen" title="Selahattin Ülkümen">
        Selahattin Ülkümen
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Jewish community of Rhodes
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
        <a href="#cite_note-43">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
       goes back to the first century AD.
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Kahal_Shalom_Synagogue" title="Kahal Shalom Synagogue">
         Kahal Shalom Synagogue
        </a>
       </i>
       , established in 1557, during the
       <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">
        Ottoman
       </a>
       era, is the oldest synagogue in Greece and still stands in the Jewish quarter of the old town of Rhodes. At its peak in the 1920s, the Jewish community was one-third of the town's total population.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
        <a href="#cite_note-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In the 1940s, there were about 2000 Jews of various ethnic backgrounds. The Nazis deported and killed most of the community during the
       <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust" title="The Holocaust">
        Holocaust
       </a>
       .
       <i>
        Kahal Shalom
       </i>
       has been renovated with the help of foreign donors but few Jews live year-round in Rhodes today, so services are not held on a regular basis.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
        <a href="#cite_note-45">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Jewish_Museum_of_Rhodes" title="Jewish Museum of Rhodes">
        Jewish Museum of Rhodes
       </a>
       was established in 1997 to preserve the Jewish history and culture of the Jews of Rhodes. It is adjacent to the
       <a href="/wiki/Kahal_Shalom_Synagogue" title="Kahal Shalom Synagogue">
        Kahal Shalom Synagogue
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Government">
        Government
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [

         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Archangelos042.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Archangelos042.JPG/220px-Archangelos042.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Archangelos042.JPG/330px-Archangelos042.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Archangelos042.JPG/440px-Archangelos042.JPG 2x" width="220"/>

         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2046" data-file-width="3210" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Lindos_Rhodes.jpg/220px-Lindos_Rhodes.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Lindos_Rhodes.jpg/330px-Lindos_Rhodes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Lindos_Rhodes.jpg/440px-Lindos_Rhodes.jpg 2x" width="220"/>

         with the Acropolis.

        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rodi_-_Spiaggia_04.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Rodi_-_Spiaggia_04.JPG/220px-Rodi_-_Spiaggia_04.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Rodi_-_Spiaggia_04.JPG/330px-Rodi_-_Spiaggia_04.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Rodi_-_Spiaggia_04.JPG/440px-Rodi_-_Spiaggia_04.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>

         <div class="magnify">

         St Paul's Bay, Lindos.

      <p>
       The present municipality Rhodes was formed at the 2011 local government reform by the merger of the following 10 former municipalities, that became municipal units (constituent communities in parentheses):
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kallikratis_2-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Kallikratis-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Afantou" title="Afantou">
         Afantou
        </a>
        (Afantou, Archipoli)
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Archangelos,_Rhodes" title="Archangelos, Rhodes">
         Archangelos
        </a>
        (Archangelos, Malonas, Masari)
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Attavyros_(municipality)" title="Attavyros (municipality)">
         Attavyros
        </a>
        (Embonas, Kritinia, Monolithos, Siana, Agios Isidoros)
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Ialysos" title="Ialysos">
         Ialysos
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Kallithea,_Rhodes" title="Kallithea, Rhodes">
         Kallithea
        </a>
        (Kalythies, Koskinou, Psinthos)
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Kameiros_(municipality)" title="Kameiros (municipality)">
         Kameiros
        </a>
        (Soroni, Apollona, Dimylia, Kalavarda, Platania, Salakos, Fanes)
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Lindos" title="Lindos">
         Lindos
        </a>
        (Lindos, Kalathos, Laerma, Lardos, Pylona)
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Petaloudes" title="Petaloudes">
         Petaloudes
        </a>
        (Kremasti, Pastida, Maritsa, Paradeisi, Theologos, Damatria)
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Rhodes_(city)" title="Rhodes (city)">
         Rhodes
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/South_Rhodes" title="South Rhodes">
         South Rhodes
        </a>
        (Gennadi, Apolakkia, Arnitha, Asklipieio, Vati, Istrios, Kattavia, Lachania,
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
         <a href="#cite_note-46">
          [46]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <a href="/wiki/Mesanagros" title="Mesanagros">
         Mesanagros
        </a>
        , Profilia)
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       The municipality has an area of 1400.681 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stat01_47-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-stat01-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It covers the island of Rhodes and a few uninhabited offshore islets. Rhodes city was the capital of the former
       <a href="/wiki/Dodecanese" title="Dodecanese">
        Dodecanese
       </a>
       Prefecture. Rhodes is the most populated island of the
       <a href="/wiki/South_Aegean" title="South Aegean">
        South Aegean
       </a>
       Region.
      </p>
