      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">
        Economy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rhodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Economy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hafenmarkt_Rhodos01.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1795" data-file-width="2894" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Hafenmarkt_Rhodos01.jpg/220px-Hafenmarkt_Rhodos01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Hafenmarkt_Rhodos01.jpg/330px-Hafenmarkt_Rhodos01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Hafenmarkt_Rhodos01.jpg/440px-Hafenmarkt_Rhodos01.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hafenmarkt_Rhodos01.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         View of the Market (Nea Agora) of Mandraki (Rhodes city), built during the Italian period.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The economy is tourist-oriented, and the most developed sector is service. Tourism has elevated Rhodes economically, compared to the rest of Greece.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
        <a href="#cite_note-48">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Small industries process imported raw materials for local retail, though other industry includes agricultural goods production, stockbreeding, fishery and winery.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">
        Transportation
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rhodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Transportation">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Air">
        Air
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rhodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Air">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Airpoort_rhodes_02.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Airpoort_rhodes_02.JPG/220px-Airpoort_rhodes_02.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Airpoort_rhodes_02.JPG/330px-Airpoort_rhodes_02.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Airpoort_rhodes_02.JPG/440px-Airpoort_rhodes_02.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Airpoort_rhodes_02.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Diagoras Airport, arrivals terminal.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Rhodes has three airports but only one is public. Diagoras Airport, one of the biggest in Greece, is the main entrance/exit point for both locals and tourists. The island is well connected with other major Greek cities and islands as well as with major European capitals and cities via charter flights.
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rhodes_International_Airport,_%22Diagoras%22" title='Rhodes International Airport, "Diagoras"'>
         Rhodes International Airport, "Diagoras"
        </a>
        : public airport, 14 km (9 mi) southwest of
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rhodes_City" title="Rhodes City">
         Rhodes City
        </a>
        , third in international passenger volume and fourth in total passenger volume in Greece.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rhodes_Maritsa_Airport" title="Rhodes Maritsa Airport">
         Rhodes Maritsa Airport
        </a>
        : closed to public, near Maritsa village. Built in 1938 by the Italians, it was the first airport of the island and was the public airport until 1977. Nowadays, it serves the
        <a href="/wiki/Hellenic_Air_Force" title="Hellenic Air Force">
         Hellenic Air Force
        </a>
        and is sometimes used for car races.
       </li>
       <li>
        Kalathos Airfield: inoperative, 7 km (4 mi) north of
        <a href="/wiki/Lindos" title="Lindos">
         Lindos
        </a>
        . Built by the Italians during World War II, was called
        <i>
         Aeroporto di Gadurrà
        </i>
        . Today only the runway is visible.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Kattavia" title="Kattavia">
         Kattavia
        </a>
        Airstrip, located in the south of the island it was an emergency airstrip built by the Italians during
        <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">
         World War II
        </a>
        . Today it is abandoned.
        <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">
         [
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">
           <span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (May 2011)">
            clarification needed
           </span>
          </a>
         </i>
         ]
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Two pilot schools offer aviation services (small plane rental and island hopping).
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sea">
        Sea
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rhodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Sea">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Louis_Majesty_Rhodes_2.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2832" data-file-width="4272" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Louis_Majesty_Rhodes_2.jpg/220px-Louis_Majesty_Rhodes_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Louis_Majesty_Rhodes_2.jpg/330px-Louis_Majesty_Rhodes_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Louis_Majesty_Rhodes_2.jpg/440px-Louis_Majesty_Rhodes_2.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Louis_Majesty_Rhodes_2.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         "
         <a href="/wiki/MS_Thomson_Majesty" title="MS Thomson Majesty">
          MS Thomson Majesty
         </a>
         " at the harbour of Rhodes.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rhodes_SkalaKamirou_tango7174.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Rhodes_SkalaKamirou_tango7174.jpg/220px-Rhodes_SkalaKamirou_tango7174.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Rhodes_SkalaKamirou_tango7174.jpg/330px-Rhodes_SkalaKamirou_tango7174.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Rhodes_SkalaKamirou_tango7174.jpg/440px-Rhodes_SkalaKamirou_tango7174.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rhodes_SkalaKamirou_tango7174.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The Kameiros Skala Dock.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Rhodes has five ports, three of them in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rhodes_City" title="Rhodes City">
        Rhodes City
       </a>
       , one in the west coast near
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kamiros" title="Kamiros">
        Kamiros
       </a>
       and one in east coast near
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Lardos&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Lardos (page does not exist)">
        Lardos
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2013)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Central Port: located in the city of Rhodes serves exclusively international traffic consisting of scheduled services to/from Turkey, cruise ships and yachts. Since Summer 2012, the port is also a homeport for Costa Cruises during the summer period.
       </li>
       <li>
        Kolona Port: opposite and north of the central port, serves intra-Dodecanese traffic and all sizes yachts.
       </li>
       <li>
        Akandia Port: the new port of the island, south and next to the central port, being built since the 1960s, for domestic, cargo and general purpose traffic. No land facilities exist although the municipality is in the process of erecting a passenger terminal.
       </li>
       <li>
        Kamiros Skala Dock: 30 km (19 mi) south west of the city near
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ancient_Kamiros" title="Ancient Kamiros">
         Ancient Kamiros
        </a>
        ruins serves mainly the island of
        <a href="/wiki/Halki_(Greece)" title="Halki (Greece)">
         Halki
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Lardos Dock: formerly servicing local industries, now under development as an alternative port for times when the central port is inaccessible due to weather conditions. It is situated in a rocky shore near the village of Lardos in south east Rhodes.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Road_network">
        Road network
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rhodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Road network">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The road network of the island is mostly paved.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2013)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       There are four major arteries:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Rhodes-Kamiros Province Avenue: Two lane, runs through the west coast north to south and connects Rhodes City with
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diagoras_Airport" title="Diagoras Airport">
         Diagoras Airport
        </a>
        and
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kamiros" title="Kamiros">
         Kamiros
        </a>
        .
        <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
         [
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
           <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2013)">
            citation needed
           </span>
          </a>
         </i>
         ]
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        Rhodes-Lindos National Avenue (
        <a href="/wiki/Greek_National_Road_95" title="Greek National Road 95">
         Greek National Road 95
        </a>
        ): Four and two lane, runs mainly inland north to south and connects Rhodes City with Lindos.
        <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
         [
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
           <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2013)">
            citation needed
           </span>
          </a>
         </i>
         ]
        </sup>
        Part from Rhodes Town until Kolympia is now 4 lanes, the rest until Lindos is 2 lanes.
       </li>
       <li>
        Rhodes-Kallithea Province Avenue: Two lanes, runs through the east coast north to south and connects Rhodes City with Faliraki Resort.
        <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
         [
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
           <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2013)">
            citation needed
           </span>
          </a>
         </i>
         ]
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        Tsairi-Airport National Avenue: Four and two lane, runs inland east to west and connects the east coast with the west and the airport.
        <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
         [
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
           <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2013)">
            citation needed
           </span>
          </a>
         </i>
         ]
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        Lindos-Katavia Province Avenue: Two lane, begins just before Lindos and though villages and resorts leads to Katavia village, the southernmost of the island, from where a further deviation leads to Prasonissi.
        <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
         [
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
           <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2013)">
            citation needed
           </span>
          </a>
         </i>
         ]
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        Rhodes Town
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ring_Road" title="Ring Road">
         Ring Road
        </a>
        : First part beginning from the new marina and ending to Rhodes-Kallithea province avenue is now almost complete as a four lane expressway. Traffic lights will be installed till the end of 2013 which will mark the completion of the road making left turns available.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Future roads:
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="needs concrete announcement for cite. Otherwise WP:CRYSTAL (September 2013)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Further widening of E-95
        <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">
         [
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">
           <span title="called Greek National Road 95 above. Need consistency (September 2013)">
            clarification needed
           </span>
          </a>
         </i>
         ]
        </sup>
        from Kolympia to Lindos. This is to be four lane with a
        <a href="/wiki/Jersey_barrier" title="Jersey barrier">
         jersey barrier
        </a>
        in the middle. It is still unknown when constructions will begin and most importantly end.
       </li>
       <li>
        Plans also exist for a new four lane express road connecting Rhodes Town with Diagoras Airport that is intended to relieve congestion on the coastal west avenue.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Bus">
        Bus
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rhodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Bus">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Bus services are handled by two operators:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
        <a href="#cite_note-49">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        RODA:
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rhodes_City" title="Rhodes City">
         Rhodes City
        </a>
        company that also services suburban areas (Faliraki, Ialysos, Kremasti, Airport, Pastida, Maritsa, Paradeisi) and the west coast of the island
       </li>
       <li>
        KTEL: State-owned buses that serve villages and resorts in the east coast of the island
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Cars_and_motorbikes">
        Cars and motorbikes
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rhodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Cars and motorbikes">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Families in Rhodes often own more than one car, along with a motorbike. Traffic jams are common particularly in the summer months. The island is served by 450 taxis.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">
        Sports
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rhodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Sports">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rhodos003.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Rhodos003.JPG/220px-Rhodos003.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Rhodos003.JPG/330px-Rhodos003.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Rhodos003.JPG/440px-Rhodos003.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rhodos003.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Diagoras_Stadium" title="Diagoras Stadium">
          Diagoras Stadium
         </a>
         in the city of Rhodes.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Football:
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AS_Rodos" title="AS Rodos">
         AS Rodos
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Diagoras_F.C." title="Diagoras F.C.">
         Diagoras F.C.
        </a>
        are the island's biggest teams and rivals. Both used to compete at the national level until a couple of years ago reaching National B' division but currently both compete at the first-tier local level. Local football leagues (organized at the prefecture level) contain three divisions with more than 50 teams.
        <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
         [
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
           <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2013)">
            citation needed
           </span>
          </a>
         </i>
         ]
        </sup>
        Many stadia are grass covered.
        <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
         [
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
           <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2013)">
            citation needed
           </span>
          </a>
         </i>
         ]
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        Basketball:
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kolossos_Rodou_BC" title="Kolossos Rodou BC">
         Colossus BC
        </a>
        sponsors professional basketball and currently plays in the top-level
        <a href="/wiki/Greek_Basket_League" title="Greek Basket League">
         Greek Basket League
        </a>
        . The local league includes two divisions with 14 teams.
        <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
         [
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
           <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2013)">
            citation needed
           </span>
          </a>
         </i>
         ]
        </sup>
        Two indoor courts exist in Rhodes City, and one each in Ialysos and Kremasti.
        <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
         [
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
           <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2013)">
            citation needed
           </span>
          </a>
         </i>
         ]
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        Volleyball: local teams only.
       </li>
       <li>
        Water polo: mostly amateur based. There is not any single indoor pool on the island.
       </li>
       <li>
        Rugby: introduced in 2007. Teams compete at the national level.
        <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
         [
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
           <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2013)">
            citation needed
           </span>
          </a>
         </i>
         ]
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        Tennis: tennis has a long history on the island.
        <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
         [
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
           <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2013)">
            citation needed
           </span>
          </a>
         </i>
         ]
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        Sailing: Island has competed at the international level
        <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
         [
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
           <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2013)">
            citation needed
           </span>
          </a>
         </i>
         ]
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        Cycling: for a long period of time Rhodes had the only cycling track in Greece, producing Olympics-level competitors.
        <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
         [
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
           <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2013)">
            citation needed
           </span>
          </a>
         </i>
         ]
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        Rhodes competes in the bi-annual
        <a href="/wiki/International_Island_Games_Association" title="International Island Games Association">
         Island Games
        </a>
        , which it hosted in 2007.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
         <a href="#cite_note-50">
          [50]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">
        Culture
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rhodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Culture">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pitaroudia.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Pitaroudia.jpg/200px-Pitaroudia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Pitaroudia.jpg/300px-Pitaroudia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Pitaroudia.jpg/400px-Pitaroudia.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pitaroudia.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <i>
          Pitaroudia
         </i>
         , a traditional chickpea dumpling from Rhodes and Dodecanese.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Local specialities of Rhodes include:
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Avranies&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Avranies (page does not exist)">
        avranies
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Koulouria&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Koulouria (page does not exist)">
        koulouria
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Pouggia&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Pouggia (page does not exist)">
        pouggia
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Tsirigia&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Tsirigia (page does not exist)">
        tsirigia
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Fanouropita&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Fanouropita (page does not exist)">
        fanouropita
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Katimeria&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Katimeria (page does not exist)">
        katimeria
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Melekouni&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Melekouni (page does not exist)">
        melekouni
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Pouggakia&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Pouggakia (page does not exist)">
        pouggakia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Takakia" title="Takakia">
        takakia
       </a>
       , or
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Mantinades&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Mantinades (page does not exist)">
        mantinades
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Muchalebi&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Muchalebi (page does not exist)">
        muchalebi
       </a>
       and pitaroudia.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2014)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       The pitaroudia is a large
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chick_pea" title="Chick pea">
        chick pea
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Fritter" title="Fritter">
        fritter
       </a>
       , and is a characteristic dish in Rhodes.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
        <a href="#cite_note-51">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">
        Notable people
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>

         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:162px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Diagoras_of_Rodes.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="350" data-file-width="233" height="240" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Diagoras_of_Rodes.jpg/160px-Diagoras_of_Rodes.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/11/Diagoras_of_Rodes.jpg 1.5x" width="160"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Diagoras_of_Rodes.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Diagoras_of_Rhodes" title="Diagoras of Rhodes">
          Diagoras of Rhodes
         </a>
         carried in the stadium by his two sons.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <ul>
       <li>

       </li>

       </li>

        <a href="/wiki/Hipparchus" title="Hipparchus">

        </a>

        </a>
        (2nd century BC), athlete
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Memnon_of_Rhodes" title="Memnon of Rhodes">
         Memnon
        </a>

       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Mentor_of_Rhodes" title="Mentor of Rhodes">
         Mentor
        </a>
        (385-340 BC), mercenary soldier, brother of Memnon
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Panaetius" title="Panaetius">
         Panaetius
        </a>
        (c. 185 - c. 110/109 BC), Stoic philosopher
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Timocreon" title="Timocreon">

        </a>
        (5th century BC), poet
       </li>

        <a href="/wiki/Joannicius_II_of_Constantinople" title="Joannicius II of Constantinople">
         Joannicius II of Constantinople
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Ecumenical_Patriarch_of_Constantinople" title="Ecumenical Patriarch of Constantinople">
         Ecumenical Patriarch of Constantinople
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Re%C5%9Fit_Galip" title="Reşit Galip">
         Reşit Galip
        </a>
        , Turkish politician, one of the first ministers of education of the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_Turkey" title="Republic of Turkey">
         Republic of Turkey
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Niki_Xanthou" title="Niki Xanthou">

        , long jumper
       </li>

        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nick_Galis" title="Nick Galis">

         FIBA Hall of Fame
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Naismith_Memorial_Basketball_Hall_of_Fame" title="Naismith Memorial Basketball Hall of Fame">
         Naismith Memorial Basketball Hall of Fame
        </a>
        member (his father was born in a small village called
        <a href="/wiki/Agios_Isidoros,_Rhodes" title="Agios Isidoros, Rhodes">
         Agios Isidoros
        </a>
        )
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Braith_Anasta" title="Braith Anasta">
         Braith Anasta
        </a>
        , rugby league player and
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NRL" title="NRL">
         NRL
        </a>
        premiership winner (ancestral ties to the island through his father, Petros ("Peter") Anastasakis)
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">
        Tourism
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rhodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Tourism">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Rhodes is one of the most attractive tourist destinations in Greece. After
       <a href="/wiki/Crete" title="Crete">
        Crete
       </a>
       the island is the most visited destination in Greece, with arrivals standing at 1.785.305 in 2013. In 2014 they stood at 1.931.005, while in 2015 the arrival number reduced slightly and stood at 1.901.000. The average length of stay is estimated at 8 days. Guests from Great Britain, Israel, France, Italy, Sweden and Norway are the ones that constitute the biggest portion in terms of the arrivals by country.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sete.gr_52-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-sete.gr-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In Rhodes the supply of available rooms is high, since more than 550 hotels are operating in the island, the majority of which are 2 star hotels.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sete.gr_52-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-sete.gr-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Additionally, in terms of competitiveness, the World Tourism Organization ranks Greece in the 31st position globally.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
        <a href="#cite_note-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
